<th scope="row">Website</th>
<td><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.sevilla.org">www<wbr />.sevilla<wbr />.org</a></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Seville</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_English" title="Help:IPA for English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/ 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/ primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ɪ/ short 'i' in 'bid'">ɪ</span><span title="'l' in 'lie'">l</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language" title="Spanish language">Spanish</a>: <span lang="es"><i>Sevilla</i></span> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[seˈβiʝa]</a></span>, <small>locally:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[seˈβi(ɟ)ʝa]</a></span><small class="nowrap metadata">&#160;(<a href="/wiki/File:Sevilla.ogg" title="File:Sevilla.ogg"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/13px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png" width="13" height="13" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/20px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/Speaker_Icon.svg/26px-Speaker_Icon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="500" /></a> <a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/fd/Sevilla.ogg" class="internal" title="Sevilla.ogg">listen</a>)</small>) is the capital and largest city of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Seville" title="Province of Seville">province of Seville</a>, Spain. It is situated on the plain of the river <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a>. The inhabitants of the city are known as <i>sevillanos</i> (feminine form: <i>sevillanas</i>) or <i>hispalenses</i>, after the <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Roman</a> name of the city, <i>Hispalis</i>. Seville has a municipal population of about 703,000 as of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, and a <a href="/wiki/List_of_metropolitan_areas_in_Spain" title="List of metropolitan areas in Spain">metropolitan</a> population of about 1.5 million, making it the <a href="/wiki/List_of_municipalities_of_Spain" title="List of municipalities of Spain">fourth-largest city in Spain</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Largest_cities_of_the_European_Union_by_population_within_city_limits" class="mw-redirect" title="Largest cities of the European Union by population within city limits">30th most populous municipality</a> in the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. Its <a href="/wiki/Old_Town" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Town">Old Town</a>, with an area of 4 square kilometres (2&#160;sq&#160;mi), contains three <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Sites" class="mw-redirect" title="World Heritage Sites">World Heritage Sites</a>: the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar palace complex</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Cathedral</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Archivo_General_de_Indias" class="mw-redirect" title="Archivo General de Indias">General Archive of the Indies</a>. The Seville harbour, located about 80 kilometres (50 miles) from the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, is the only river port in Spain. Seville is also the hottest major metropolitan area in the geographical <a href="/wiki/Western_Europe" title="Western Europe">Western Europe</a>, with summer average high temperatures of above 35&#160;°C (95&#160;°F).</p>
<p>Seville was founded as the Roman city of <i>Hispalis</i>. It later became known as <i>Ishbiliya</i><sup id="cite_ref-JayyusiMar.C3.ADn1992_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JayyusiMar.C3.ADn1992-2">[2]</a></sup> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl"><span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-family:Harmattan,Scheherazade,Lateef,Alkalami,Amiri,'DejaVu Sans',FreeSerif,'Noto Naskh Arabic','Droid Arabic Naskh','Arabic Typesetting','Sakkal Majalla','Traditional Arabic','Simplified Arabic','Caribri','Segoe UI','Microsoft Sans Serif',Arial,'Times New Roman',serif,sans-serif; font-size: 125%; font-weight:normal;">إشبيلية‎</span></span>‎‎) after the Muslim conquest in 712. During the Muslim rule in Spain, Seville came under the jurisdiction of the <a href="/wiki/Caliphate_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Caliphate of Córdoba">Caliphate of Córdoba</a> before becoming the independent <a href="/wiki/Taifa_of_Seville" title="Taifa of Seville">Taifa of Seville</a>; later it was ruled by the Muslim <a href="/wiki/Almoravids" class="mw-redirect" title="Almoravids">Almoravids</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad dynasty">Almohads</a> until finally being incorporated into the Christian <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Castile" title="Kingdom of Castile">Kingdom of Castile</a> under <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand III of Castile">Ferdinand III</a> in 1248.<sup id="cite_ref-Christian-Muslim_Relations._A_Bibliographical_History._Volume_4_.281200.E2.80.931350.29_3-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Christian-Muslim_Relations._A_Bibliographical_History._Volume_4_.281200.E2.80.931350.29-3">[3]</a></sup> After the discovery of the Americas, Seville became one of the economic centres of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Empire" title="Spanish Empire">Spanish Empire</a> as its port monopolised the trans-oceanic trade and the <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Contrataci%C3%B3n" title="Casa de Contratación">Casa de Contratación</a> (House of Trade) wielded its power, opening a <a href="/wiki/Golden_Age_of_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Age of Spain">Golden Age</a> of arts and literature. In 1519, <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> departed from Seville for the first circumnavigation of the Earth. Coinciding with the Baroque period of European history, the 17th century in Seville represented the most brilliant flowering of the city's culture; then began a gradual economic and demographic decline as silting in the <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a> forced the trade monopoly to relocate to the nearby port of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>.</p>
<p>The 20th century in Seville saw the tribulations of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>, decisive cultural milestones such as the <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Exposition_of_1929" title="Ibero-American Exposition of 1929">Ibero-American Exposition of 1929</a> and <a href="/wiki/Seville_Expo_%2792" title="Seville Expo '92">Expo '92</a>, and the city's election as the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Autonomous_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalusian Autonomous Government">Autonomous Community of Andalusia</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Name">Name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Name">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Spal</i> is the oldest known name for Seville. It appears to have originated during the <a href="/wiki/Phoenicia" title="Phoenicia">Phoenician</a> colonisation of the <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">Tartessian</a> culture in south-western Iberia and, according to Manuel Pellicer Catalán, meant "lowland" in the <a href="/wiki/Phoenician_language" title="Phoenician language">Phoenician language</a> (similar to the Hebrew <a href="/wiki/Shfela" title="Shfela">Shfela</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-SPAL:_Revista_de_prehistoria_y_arqueolog.C3.ADa_de_la_Universidad_de_Sevilla_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SPAL:_Revista_de_prehistoria_y_arqueolog.C3.ADa_de_la_Universidad_de_Sevilla-4">[4]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> During <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">Roman</a> rule, the name was Latinised as <i>Hispalis</i>. After the Umayyad invasion, this name was adapted into Arabic as <i>Ishbiliyya</i> (<a href="/wiki/Arabic" title="Arabic">Arabic</a> <span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-family:Harmattan,Scheherazade,Lateef,Alkalami,Amiri,'DejaVu Sans',FreeSerif,'Noto Naskh Arabic','Droid Arabic Naskh','Arabic Typesetting','Sakkal Majalla','Traditional Arabic','Simplified Arabic','Caribri','Segoe UI','Microsoft Sans Serif',Arial,'Times New Roman',serif,sans-serif; font-size: 125%; font-weight:normal;">إشبيلية‎</span>); since <i>p</i> does not exist in Arabic, it was replaced by <i>b</i>, the Latin place-name suffix <i>-is</i> was replaced by its direct Arabic equivalent <i>-iyya</i>, and stressed <i>a</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/æ/</span> turned into <i>i</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA">/i/</span>, due to the phonetic phenomenon called <a href="/wiki/Im%C4%81la" title="Imāla">imāla</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Motto">Motto</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Motto">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>"NO8DO" is the official motto of Seville. It is popularly believed to be a <a href="/wiki/Rebus" title="Rebus">rebus</a> signifying the Spanish "No me ha dejado", meaning "It [Seville] has not abandoned me" but pronounced with <a href="/wiki/Synalepha" title="Synalepha">synalepha</a> as <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[no ma ðeˈxaðo]</a></span> . The eight in the middle represents a <i>madeja</i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_Spanish" title="Help:IPA for Spanish">[maˈðexa]</a></span>, or skein of wool. Legend states that the title was given by King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X" class="mw-redirect" title="Alfonso X">Alfonso X</a>, who was resident in the city's <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a> and supported by the citizens when his son, later <a href="/wiki/Sancho_IV_of_Castille" class="mw-redirect" title="Sancho IV of Castille">Sancho IV of Castille</a>, tried to usurp the throne from him. The emblem is present on the municipal flag and features on city property such as manhole covers, and <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a>'s tomb in the Cathedral.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Seville" title="History of Seville">History of Seville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Seville" title="Timeline of Seville">Timeline of Seville</a></div>
<p>Seville is approximately 2,200 years old. The passage of the various civilisations instrumental in its growth has left the city with a distinct personality, and a large and well-preserved historical centre.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_periods">Early periods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Early periods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The mythological founder of the city is Hercules (<a href="/wiki/Heracles" title="Heracles">Heracles</a>), commonly identified with the Phoenician god <a href="/wiki/Melqart" title="Melqart">Melqart</a>, who the myth says sailed through the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a> to the Atlantic, and founded trading posts at the current sites of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> and of Seville.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_(7077900543).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg/220px-View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg/330px-View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/18/View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg/440px-View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_%287077900543%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="4288" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:View_from_Alc%C3%A1zar_on_Giralda_(7077900543).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
View of the <a href="/wiki/Giralda" title="Giralda">Giralda</a> from the <i>Patio de Banderas</i> (Courtyard of Flags), historic square with remains of Roman, Moorish and Castilian periods.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The city was known from <a href="/wiki/Hispania#Roman_Hispania" title="Hispania">Roman times</a> as <i>Hispalis</i>. Important archaeological remains also exist in the nearby towns of <a href="/wiki/Santiponce" title="Santiponce">Santiponce</a> (<a href="/wiki/Italica" title="Italica">Italica</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Carmona,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmona, Spain">Carmona</a>.</p>
<p>Existing Roman features in Seville include the remnants of an <a href="/wiki/Roman_aqueduct" title="Roman aqueduct">aqueduct</a>, a temple in <i>Mármoles</i> Street, the columns of <a href="/wiki/La_Alameda,_Seville" title="La Alameda, Seville">La Alameda de Hércules</a>, the remains exposed <i>in situ</i> in the underground Antiquarium of the <a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a> building and the remains in the Patio de Banderas square near of the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Seville Cathedral</a>. The walls surrounding the city were originally built during the rule of <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>, but their current course and design were the result of Moorish reconstructions.<sup id="cite_ref-degelo.com_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-degelo.com-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<p>Following Roman rule, there were successive conquests of the Roman province of <i><a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">Hispania Baetica</a></i> by the <a href="/wiki/Vandals" title="Vandals">Vandals</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Suebi" title="Suebi">Suebi</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Visigoths" title="Visigoths">Visigoths</a> during the 5th and 6th centuries.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Moorish_era">Moorish era</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Moorish era">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seville was taken by the <a href="/wiki/Moors" title="Moors">Moors</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muslim" title="Muslim">Muslims</a> from North of <a href="/wiki/Africa" title="Africa">Africa</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_conquest_of_Hispania" title="Umayyad conquest of Hispania">conquest</a> of Hispalis in 712. It was the capital for the kings of the <a href="/wiki/Umayyad_Caliphate" title="Umayyad Caliphate">Umayyad Caliphate</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Almoravid_dynasty" title="Almoravid dynasty">Almoravid dynasty</a> first and after the <a href="/wiki/Almohad_dynasty" class="mw-redirect" title="Almohad dynasty">Almohad dynasty</a> (from Arabic <span class="script-arabic script-Arab" dir="rtl" style="font-family:Harmattan,Scheherazade,Lateef,Alkalami,Amiri,'DejaVu Sans',FreeSerif,'Noto Naskh Arabic','Droid Arabic Naskh','Arabic Typesetting','Sakkal Majalla','Traditional Arabic','Simplified Arabic','Caribri','Segoe UI','Microsoft Sans Serif',Arial,'Times New Roman',serif,sans-serif; font-size: 125%; font-weight:normal;">الموحدون‎</span> al-Muwahhidun, i.e., "the monotheists" or "the Unitarians"), from the 8th to 13th centuries.</p>
<p>The Moorish urban influences continued and are present in contemporary Seville, for instance in the custom of decorating with herbaje and small fountains the courtyards of the houses. However, most buildings of the Moorish aesthetic actually belong to the <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">Mudéjar</a> style of Islamic art, developed under Christian rule and inspired by the Arabic style. Original <a href="/wiki/Moorish" class="mw-redirect" title="Moorish">Moorish</a> buildings are the <i>Patio del Yeso</i> in the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a>, the city walls, and the main section of the <a href="/wiki/Giralda" title="Giralda">Giralda</a>, bell tower of the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Seville Cathedral</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Castilian_rule">Castilian rule</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Castilian rule">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Seville" title="Siege of Seville">Siege of Seville</a></div>
<p>In 1247, the Christian King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand III of Castile">Ferdinand III of Castile</a> and Leon began the conquest of Andalusia. After conquering Jaén and Córdoba, he seized the villages surrounding the city, <a href="/wiki/Carmona,_Spain" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmona, Spain">Carmona</a> Lora del Rio and Alcalá del Rio, and kept a standing army in the vicinity, the siege lasting for fifteen months. The decisive action took place in May 1248 when Ramon Bonifaz sailed up the Guadalquivir and severed the Triana bridge that made the provisioning of the city from the farms of the <a href="/wiki/Albaida_del_Aljarafe" title="Albaida del Aljarafe">Aljarafe</a> possible. The city surrendered on 23 November 1248.<sup id="cite_ref-O.27Callaghan1975_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-O.27Callaghan1975-10">[10]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city's development continued after the <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_Castile" title="Crown of Castile">Castilian</a> conquest in 1248. Public buildings constructed including churches, many of which were built in the <i><a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">Mudéjar</a></i> style, and the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Seville Cathedral</a>, built during the 15th century with <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic architecture</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Norwich2001_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Norwich2001-11">[11]</a></sup> The Moors' Palace became the Castilian royal residence, and during <a href="/wiki/Pedro_of_Castile" class="mw-redirect" title="Pedro of Castile">Pedro I</a>'s rule it was replaced by the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a> (the upper levels are still used by the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Royal_Family" title="Spanish Royal Family">Royal Family</a> as the official Seville residence).</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:708px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_panorama.jpg" class="image" title="Cathedral of Saint Mary from Constitución Avenue"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Seville_panorama.jpg/700px-Seville_panorama.jpg" width="700" height="199" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Seville_panorama.jpg/1050px-Seville_panorama.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Seville_panorama.jpg/1400px-Seville_panorama.jpg 2x" data-file-width="10782" data-file-height="3060" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_panorama.jpg" title="File:Seville panorama.jpg"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of seville">Cathedral of Saint Mary</a> from Constitución Avenue</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg/220px-Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg/330px-Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/70/Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg/440px-Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3424" data-file-height="2262" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Patio_de_las_doncellas.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Courtyard of the Maidens in the <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar of Seville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the 1391 <a href="/wiki/Pogrom" title="Pogrom">Pogrom</a>, believed to having been instigated by the Archdeacon Ferrant Martinez, all the <a href="/wiki/Synagogue" title="Synagogue">synagogues</a> in Seville were converted to churches (renamed Santa María la Blanca, San Bartolome, Santa Cruz, and Convento Madre de Dios). The Jewish quarter's land and shops (sited in modern-day 'Barrio Santa Cruz') were appropriated by the church. Many were killed during the pogrom, although most were <a href="/wiki/B%27nei_Anusim" class="mw-redirect" title="B'nei Anusim">forced to convert</a>.</p>
<p>The first tribunal of the Spanish <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a> was instituted in Seville in 1478. At first, the activity of the Inquisition was limited to the dioceses of <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Archdiocese_of_Seville" title="Roman Catholic Archdiocese of Seville">Seville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_C%C3%B3rdoba" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of Córdoba">Córdoba</a>, where <a href="/wiki/Alonso_de_Hojeda" class="mw-redirect" title="Alonso de Hojeda">Alonso de Hojeda</a> had detected <a href="/wiki/Crypto-jews" class="mw-redirect" title="Crypto-jews">converso</a> activity. The first <a href="/wiki/Auto-da-f%C3%A9" title="Auto-da-fé">Auto de Fé</a> took place in Seville on 6 February 1481, when six people were burned alive. Alonso de Hojeda himself gave the sermon. The Inquisition then grew rapidly. The Plaza de San Francisco was the site of the 'autos de fé'. By 1492, tribunals existed in eight Castilian cities: Ávila, Córdoba, Jaén, Medina del Campo, Segovia, Sigüenza, Toledo and Valladolid;<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> and by the <a href="/wiki/Alhambra_decree" class="mw-redirect" title="Alhambra decree">Alhambra decree</a> all Jews were <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">forced to convert</a> to Catholicism or be ejected from Spain.<sup id="cite_ref-Levine_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Levine-13">[13]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Golden_Age">The Golden Age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: The Golden Age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/350px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg" width="350" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/525px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f6/La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg/700px-La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1500" data-file-height="747" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:La_sevilla_del_sigloXVI.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Seville in the 16th century</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following the 1492 <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> expedition to the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> (from the port of <a href="/wiki/Palos_de_la_Frontera" title="Palos de la Frontera">Palos de la Frontera</a>), the results from his claiming territory and trade for the Crown of Castile (incipient Spain) in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> began to profit the city, as all goods imported from the New World had to pass through the <a href="/wiki/Casa_de_Contratacion" class="mw-redirect" title="Casa de Contratacion">Casa de Contratacion</a> before being distributed throughout the rest of Spain. A 'golden age of development' commenced in Seville, due to its being the only port awarded the royal monopoly for trade with the growing <a href="/wiki/Spanish_colonisation_of_the_Americas" class="mw-redirect" title="Spanish colonisation of the Americas">Spanish colonies in the Americas</a> and the influx of riches from them. Since only <a href="/wiki/Winds_in_the_Age_of_Sail" title="Winds in the Age of Sail">sailing ships</a> leaving from and returning to the inland port of Seville could engage in trade with the <a href="/wiki/European_colonization_of_the_Americas" title="European colonization of the Americas">Spanish Americas</a>, merchants from Europe and other trade centres needed to go to Seville to acquire <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> trade goods. The city's population grew to more than a hundred thousand people.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the late 16th century the monopoly was broken, with the port of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> also authorised as a port of trade. The <a href="/wiki/Great_Plague_of_Seville" title="Great Plague of Seville">Great Plague of Seville</a> in 1649 reduced the population by almost half, and it would not recover until the early 19th century.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> By the 18th century its international importance was in decline. After the silting up of the harbour by the <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a> (river), upriver shipping ceased and the city went into relative economic decline.</p>
<p>The writer <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a> lived primarily in Seville between 1596 and 1600. Because of financial problems, Cervantes worked as a purveyor for the Spanish Armada, and later as a tax collector. In 1597, discrepancies in his accounts of the three years previous landed him in the Royal Prison of Seville for a short time. <i><a href="/wiki/Rinconete_y_Cortadillo" title="Rinconete y Cortadillo">Rinconete y Cortadillo</a></i>, a popular comedy among his works, features two young vagabonds who come to Seville, attracted by the riches and disorder that the 16th-century commerce with the Americas had brought to that metropolis.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_century">18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_Sevilla_(rectorado)_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg/220px-Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg/330px-Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg/440px-Universidad_de_Sevilla_%28rectorado%29_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Universidad_de_Sevilla_(rectorado)_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Royal_Tobacco_Factory" title="Royal Tobacco Factory">Royal Tobacco Factory</a>, today <a href="/wiki/Rector_(academia)" title="Rector (academia)">rectorate</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Seville" title="University of Seville">University of Seville</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the 18th century <a href="/wiki/Charles_III_of_Spain" title="Charles III of Spain">Charles III of Spain</a> promoted Seville's industries. Construction of the <i>Real Fábrica de Tabacos</i> (<a href="/wiki/Royal_Tobacco_Factory" title="Royal Tobacco Factory">Royal Tobacco Factory</a>) began in 1728, with additions to it over the next 30 years.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> It was the second largest building in Spain, after the royal residence <a href="/wiki/El_Escorial" title="El Escorial">El Escorial</a>. Since the 1950s it has been the seat of the rectorate of the University of Seville, together with the Schools of Law, Philology, Geography and History.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Many operas have been set in the city, including those by such composers as <a href="/wiki/Beethoven" class="mw-redirect" title="Beethoven">Beethoven</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/Fidelio" title="Fidelio">Fidelio</a>)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Mozart" class="mw-redirect" title="Mozart">Mozart</a> <i>(<a href="/wiki/The_Marriage_of_Figaro" title="The Marriage of Figaro">The Marriage of Figaro</a> and <a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a>)</i>, <a href="/wiki/Rossini" class="mw-redirect" title="Rossini">Rossini</a> (<a href="/wiki/The_Barber_of_Seville" title="The Barber of Seville">The Barber of Seville</a>) and <a href="/wiki/Bizet" class="mw-redirect" title="Bizet">Bizet</a> "(<a href="/wiki/Carmen" title="Carmen">Carmen</a>)".<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seville became the dean of the Spanish provincial press in 1758 with the publication of its first newspaper, the <i>Hebdomario útil de Seville</i>, the first to be printed in Spain outside Madrid.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_and_20th_centuries">19th and 20th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 19th and 20th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG/220px-Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG/330px-Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG/440px-Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1536" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Puente_de_Triana_iluminado.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>The Isabel II bridge</i>, better known as the <b>Triana Bridge</b></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Between 1825 and 1833, Melchor Cano acted as chief architect in Seville; most of the urban planning policy and architectural modifications of the city were made by him and his collaborator Jose Manuel Arjona y Cuba.<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>Industrial architecture surviving today from the first half of the 19th century includes the ceramics factory installed in the Carthusian monastery at La Cartuja in 1841 by the Pickman family, and now home to the El Centro Andaluz de Arte Contemporáneo (CAAC),<sup id="cite_ref-al_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-al-19">[19]</a></sup> which manages the collections of the Museo de Arte Contemporáneo de Sevilla.<sup id="cite_ref-NavarroTorres2002_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NavarroTorres2002-20">[20]</a></sup> It also houses the rectory of the UNIA.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>In the years that <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Queen Isabel II</a> ruled directly, about 1843–1868, the Sevillian bourgeoisie invested in a construction boom unmatched in the city's history. The Isabel II bridge, better known as the Triana bridge, dates from this period; street lighting was expanded in the municipality and most of the streets were paved during this time as well.<sup id="cite_ref-A_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p>By the second half of the 19th century Seville began an expansion supported by railway construction and the demolition of part of its ancient walls, allowing the urban space of the city to grow eastward and southward. The <i>Sevillana de Electricidad</i> Company was created in 1894 to provide electric power throughout the municipality,<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> and in 1901 the <i>Plaza de Armas</i> railway station was inaugurated. The Museum of Fine Arts <i>(Museo de Bellas Artes de Sevilla)</i> opened in 1904.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fuente_de_Sevilla_fountain_at_the_Puerta_de_Jerez_square_(a_tower_of_Hotel_Alfonso_XIII_building_in_the_background)._Seville,_Andalusia,_Spain,_Southwestern_Europe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/The_Fuente_de_Sevilla_fountain_at_the_Puerta_de_Jerez_square_%28a_tower_of_Hotel_Alfonso_XIII_building_in_the_background%29._Seville%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain%2C_Southwestern_Europe.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/The_Fuente_de_Sevilla_fountain_at_the_Puerta_de_Jerez_square_%28a_tower_of_Hotel_Alfonso_XIII_building_in_the_background%29._Seville%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain%2C_Southwestern_Europe.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/The_Fuente_de_Sevilla_fountain_at_the_Puerta_de_Jerez_square_%28a_tower_of_Hotel_Alfonso_XIII_building_in_the_background%29._Seville%2C_Andalusia%2C_Spain%2C_Southwestern_Europe.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2008" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Fuente_de_Sevilla_fountain_at_the_Puerta_de_Jerez_square_(a_tower_of_Hotel_Alfonso_XIII_building_in_the_background)._Seville,_Andalusia,_Spain,_Southwestern_Europe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The "Fountain of Hispalis (Roman Seville)" and the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Alfonso_XIII" title="Hotel Alfonso XIII">Alfonso XIII Hotel</a>, built for the <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Exposition_of_1929" title="Ibero-American Exposition of 1929">Ibero-American Exposition of 1929</a>, in Puerta de Jerez.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1929 the city hosted the <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Exposition_of_1929" title="Ibero-American Exposition of 1929">Ibero-American Exposition</a>, which accelerated the southern expansion of the city and created new public spaces such as the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Seville)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza de España (Seville)">Plaza de España</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Maria_Luisa_Park" title="Maria Luisa Park">Maria Luisa Park</a>. Not long before the opening, the Spanish government began a modernisation of the city in order to prepare for the expected crowds by erecting new hotels and widening the mediaeval streets to allow for the movement of automobiles.<sup id="cite_ref-Luce1929_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Luce1929-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seville fell very quickly at the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a> in 1936. General <a href="/wiki/Queipo_de_Llano" class="mw-redirect" title="Queipo de Llano">Queipo de Llano</a> carried out a coup within the city, quickly capturing the city centre.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-25">[25]</a></sup> Radio Seville opposed the uprising and called for the peasants to come to the city for arms, while workers' groups established barricades.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-25">[25]</a></sup> De Llano then moved to capture Radio Seville, which he used to broadcast propaganda on behalf of the Franquist forces.<sup id="cite_ref-Thomas_25-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Thomas-25">[25]</a></sup> After the initial takeover of the city, resistance continued among residents of the working-class neighbourhoods for some time, until a series of fierce reprisals took place.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p>
<p>Under <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a>'s rule Spain was officially neutral in World War II (although it did collaborate with the <a href="/wiki/Axis_powers" title="Axis powers">Axis powers</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Payne2008_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Payne2008-27">[27]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bowen2006_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bowen2006-28">[28]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Corporation2004_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Corporation2004-29">[29]</a></sup> and like the rest of the country, Seville remained largely economically and culturally isolated from the outside world. In 1953 the shipyard of Seville was opened, eventually employing more than 2,000 workers in the 1970s. Before the existence of wetlands regulation in the Guadalquivir basin, Seville suffered regular heavy flooding; perhaps worst of all were the floods that occurred in November 1961 when the River Tamarguillo, a tributary of the Guadalquivir, overflowed as a result of a prodigious downpour of rain, and Seville was consequently declared a disaster zone.<sup id="cite_ref-PfisterBr.C3.A1zdil2013_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PfisterBr.C3.A1zdil2013-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>Trade unionism in Seville began during the 1960s with the underground organisational activities of the Workers' Commissions or Comisiones Obreras (CCOO), in factories such as Hytasa, the Astilleros shipyards, Hispano Aviación, etc. Several of the movement's leaders were imprisoned in November 1973.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 3 April 1979 Spain held its first democratic municipal elections after the end of Franco's dictatorship; councillors representing four different political parties were elected in Seville. On 5 November 1982, <a href="/wiki/Pope_John_Paul_II" title="Pope John Paul II">Pope John Paul II</a> arrived in Seville to officiate at a Mass before more than half a million people at the fairgrounds. He visited the city again 13 June 1993, for the International Eucharistic Congress.</p>
<p>In 1992, coinciding with the fifth centenary of the <a href="/wiki/Voyages_of_Christopher_Columbus" title="Voyages of Christopher Columbus">Discovery of the Americas</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Expo_%2792" title="Seville Expo '92">Universal Exposition</a> was held for six months in Seville, on the occasion of which the local communications network infrastructure was greatly improved: the SE-30 ring road around the city was completed and new highways were constructed; the new Santa Justa train station had opened in 1991, while the Spanish High Speed Rail system, the <i>Alta Velocidad Española</i> (AVE), began to operate between Madrid-Seville. The <a href="/wiki/Seville_Airport" title="Seville Airport">Seville Airport</a>, <i>(Aeropuerto de Sevilla)</i>, was expanded with a new terminal building designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Moneo" title="Rafael Moneo">Rafael Moneo</a>, and various other improvements were made. The monumental <i><a href="/wiki/Puente_del_Alamillo" title="Puente del Alamillo">Puente del Alamillo</a></i> (Alamillo Bridge) over the Guadalquivir, designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Calatrava" title="Santiago Calatrava">Santiago Calatrava</a>, was built to allow access to the island of La Cartuja, site of the massive exposition. Some of the installations remaining at the site after the exposition were converted into the Scientific and Technological Park <a href="/wiki/Cartuja_93" title="Cartuja 93">Cartuja 93</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2004 the <a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a> project, commonly known as <i>Las Setas (</i>English: <i>The Mushrooms -</i> due to the appearance of the structure), was launched to revitalise the Plaza de la Encarnación, for years used as a car park and seen as a dead spot between more popular tourist destinations in the city. The <a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a> was completed in March 2011,<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> costing just over €102 million in total, more than twice as much as originally planned.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> Constructed from crossed wooden beams, <i>Las Setas</i> is said to be the largest timber-framed structure in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:808px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg" class="image" title="Metropol Parasol, locally also known as Las Setas by the German architect Jürgen Mayer"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg/800px-Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg" width="800" height="359" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg/1200px-Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg/1600px-Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4654" data-file-height="2087" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Espacio_Parasol_Sevilla.jpg" title="File:Espacio Parasol Sevilla.jpg"></a></div>
<i><a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a></i>, locally also known as <i>Las Setas</i> by the German architect <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Mayer_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jürgen Mayer (architect)">Jürgen Mayer</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Seville has an area of 140&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (54&#160;sq&#160;mi), according to the National Topographic Map <i>(Mapa Topográfico Nacional)</i> series from the <i>Instituto Geográfico Nacional&#160;– Centro Nacional de Información Geográfica</i>, the country's civilian survey organisation (pages 984, 985 and 1002). The city is situated in the fertile valley of the Guadalquivir River. The average height <a href="/wiki/Above_mean_sea_level" class="mw-redirect" title="Above mean sea level">above sea level</a> is 7 metres (23 feet). Most of the city is on the east side of the river, while <a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville" title="Triana, Seville">Triana</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Cartuja,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="La Cartuja, Seville">La Cartuja</a> and <a href="/wiki/Los_Remedios,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Remedios, Seville">Los Remedios</a> are on the west side. The <a href="/wiki/Albaida_del_Aljarafe" title="Albaida del Aljarafe">Aljarafe</a> region lies further west, and is considered part of the metropolitan area. The city has boundaries on the north with <a href="/wiki/La_Rinconada" title="La Rinconada">La Rinconada</a>, <a href="/wiki/La_Algaba" title="La Algaba">La Algaba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Santiponce" title="Santiponce">Santiponce</a>; on the east with <a href="/wiki/Alcal%C3%A1_de_Guadaira" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcalá de Guadaira">Alcalá de Guadaira</a>; on the south with <a href="/wiki/Dos_Hermanas" title="Dos Hermanas">Dos Hermanas</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gelves" title="Gelves">Gelves</a> and on the west with <a href="/wiki/San_Juan_de_Aznalfarache" title="San Juan de Aznalfarache">San Juan de Aznalfarache</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tomares" title="Tomares">Tomares</a> and <a href="/wiki/Camas,_Seville" title="Camas, Seville">Camas</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Position">Position</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Position">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seville is on the same <a href="/wiki/37th_parallel_north" title="37th parallel north">parallel</a> as <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> west coast city <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco" title="San Francisco">San Francisco</a> and the surrounding <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco_Bay_Area" title="San Francisco Bay Area">Bay Area</a>. In addition to that <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A3o_Miguel_Island" title="São Miguel Island">São Miguel</a>, the main island of the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> archipelago lies on the same latitude. Further east from Seville in the <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_Basin" title="Mediterranean Basin">Mediterranean Basin</a>, it is on the same latitude as <a href="/wiki/Catania" title="Catania">Catania</a> of <a href="/wiki/Sicily" title="Sicily">Sicily</a>, <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> and just south of <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a>, the capital of <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>. Even further east, it is located on the same parallel as <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korean</a> capital of <a href="/wiki/Seoul" title="Seoul">Seoul</a>. Seville is located not many miles inland from the Andalusian coast, but still sees a much more continental climate than the nearest port cities <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">Huelva</a> for example—although it is much too mild in winter to be described as a 'proper' continental area. It is at a relative distance from the three larger cities in the country, as well as <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a> in <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>, making it by far the largest city in the south of the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_peninsula" class="mw-redirect" title="Iberian peninsula">Iberian peninsula</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg/220px-Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg/330px-Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg/440px-Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3076" data-file-height="2047" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Toits_Guadalquivir_ponts_S%C3%A9ville_Espagne.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Skyline of Seville from the top of the <a href="/wiki/Giralda" title="Giralda">Giralda</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville has a <a href="/wiki/Subtropical" class="mw-redirect" title="Subtropical">subtropical</a> <a href="/wiki/Mediterranean_climate" title="Mediterranean climate">Mediterranean climate</a> (<a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">Köppen climate classification</a> <i>Csa</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Like most Mediterranean climates, Seville has a drier summer and wet winter. The annual average temperature is 25.4&#160;°C (78&#160;°F) during the day and 13&#160;°C (55&#160;°F) at night. Summer is the dominant season and lasts from May to October, the latter in spite of the dwindling daylight and inland position.</p>
<p>With an annual average of 19.2&#160;°C (67&#160;°F), Seville is the warmest city on <a href="/wiki/Continental_Europe" title="Continental Europe">Continental Europe</a>. After the city of <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">Córdoba</a> (also in Andalusia), Seville has the hottest summer in continental Europe among all cities with a population over 100,000 people, with average daily highs in July of 36.0&#160;°C (97&#160;°F). Average minimum temperatures in July are 20.3&#160;°C (69&#160;°F) and every year the temperature exceeds 40&#160;°C (104&#160;°F) on several occasions. The coldest temperature extreme of −5.5&#160;°C (22&#160;°F)<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> was registered by the weather station at <a href="/wiki/Seville_Airport" title="Seville Airport">Seville Airport</a> on 12 February 1956. A historical record high (disputed) of 50.0&#160;°C (122&#160;°F) was recorded on 4 August 1881, according to the NOAA Satellite and Information Service.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> There is a non-accredited record by the National Institute of Meteorology of 47.2&#160;°C (117&#160;°F) on 1 August during the <a href="/wiki/2003_European_heat_wave" title="2003 European heat wave">2003 heat wave</a>, according to a weather station (83910 LEZL) located in the southern part of Seville Airport, near the abandoned military zone. This temperature would be one of the highest ever recorded in Spain. The average sunshine hours are approximately 3000 per year.</p>
<ul>
<li>Winters are mild: January is the coolest month, with average maximum temperatures of 16.0&#160;°C (61&#160;°F) and minimum of 5.7&#160;°C (42&#160;°F).</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Precipitation_(meteorology)" class="mw-redirect" title="Precipitation (meteorology)">Precipitation</a> varies from 400 to 650&#160;mm (15.7 to 25.6&#160;in) per year, with frequent <a href="/wiki/Torrential_rain" class="mw-redirect" title="Torrential rain">torrential rain</a>. December is the wettest month, with an average rainfall of 99 millimetres (3.9&#160;in). On average there are 50.5 days of rain.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government">Government</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Seville is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>. The historical edifice of the <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_San_Telmo" title="Palace of San Telmo">Palace of San Telmo</a> is now the seat of the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Autonomous_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalusian Autonomous Government">Andalusian Autonomous Government</a>. The administrative headquarters are in Torre Triana, in <a href="/wiki/La_Cartuja,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="La Cartuja, Seville">La Cartuja</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Hospital_de_las_Cinco_Llagas" title="Hospital de las Cinco Llagas">Hospital de las Cinco Llagas</a> (literally, "Hospital of the Five Holy Wounds") is the current seat of the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_Andalusia" title="Parliament of Andalusia">Parliament of Andalusia</a>. Since 2015 the government of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> is a coalition between the <a href="/wiki/Centre-left" class="mw-redirect" title="Centre-left">centre-left</a> <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Socialist_Workers%27_Party" title="Spanish Socialist Workers' Party">Spanish Socialist Workers' Party</a> or <i>Partido Socialista Obrero Español</i> (PSOE) and the centrist <a href="/wiki/Ciudadanos" class="mw-redirect" title="Ciudadanos">Ciudadanos</a>; its president is <a href="/wiki/Susana_D%C3%ADaz" title="Susana Díaz">Susana Díaz</a>. Elections to the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_communities_of_Spain" title="Autonomous communities of Spain">autonomous community</a> are held every four years.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Telmo_005.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/San_Telmo_005.jpg/220px-San_Telmo_005.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/San_Telmo_005.jpg/330px-San_Telmo_005.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/San_Telmo_005.jpg/440px-San_Telmo_005.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:San_Telmo_005.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Palace_of_San_Telmo" title="Palace of San Telmo">Palace of San Telmo</a>, seat of the presidency of the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Autonomous_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalusian Autonomous Government">Andalusian Autonomous Government</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Community" class="mw-redirect" title="Autonomous Community">Autonomous Community</a> of <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>, according to Article 4 of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Statute_of_Autonomy_of_Andaluc%C3%ADa&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Statute of Autonomy of Andalucía (page does not exist)">Statute of Autonomy of Andalucía</a> of 2007, and is the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Seville" title="Province of Seville">Province of Seville</a> as well.</p>
<p>The Common Council of Seville has 33 councillors and a mayor, with elections every four years. Since 2011, the government of the city has been by the conservative <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Party_(Spain)" title="People's Party (Spain)">People's Party</a> or <i>Partido Popular</i> (PP), and Juan Ignacio Zoido Álvarez has been mayor. The City Hall is on the Plaza Nueva, in the <i><a href="/wiki/El_Arenal,_Seville" title="El Arenal, Seville">El Arenal</a></i> neighbourhood. The administration of the City is decentralized into 11 districts.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Districts_and_neighbourhoods">Districts and neighbourhoods</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Districts and neighbourhoods">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Districts_and_neighbourhoods_of_Seville" title="Districts and neighbourhoods of Seville">Districts and neighbourhoods of Seville</a></div>
<p>Seville has 11 districts, further divided into 108 neighbourhoods.</p>
<div class="div-col columns column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 22em; -webkit-column-width: 22em; column-width: 22em;">
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Casco_Antiguo" title="Casco Antiguo">Casco Antiguo</a></li>
<li>Distrito Sur</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville" title="Triana, Seville">Triana</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Macarena,_Seville" title="Macarena, Seville">Macarena</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Nervi%C3%B3n,_Seville" title="Nervión, Seville">Nervión</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Los_Remedios,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Remedios, Seville">Los Remedios</a></li>
<li>Este-Alcosa-Torreblanca</li>
<li>Cerro-Amate</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Bellavista-La_Palmera" title="Bellavista-La Palmera">Bellavista-La Palmera</a></li>
<li>San Pablo-Santa Justa</li>
</ul>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/File:Distritos_Sevilla.svg" class="image"><img alt="Distritos Sevilla.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Distritos_Sevilla.svg/574px-Distritos_Sevilla.svg.png" width="574" height="511" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Distritos_Sevilla.svg/861px-Distritos_Sevilla.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Distritos_Sevilla.svg/1148px-Distritos_Sevilla.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="574" data-file-height="511" /></a></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Main_sights">Main sights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Main sights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Sights_and_landmarks_of_Seville" title="Sights and landmarks of Seville">Sights and landmarks of Seville</a></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">Cathedral</a>, and the <i><a href="/wiki/Archivo_General_de_Indias" class="mw-redirect" title="Archivo General de Indias">Archivo General de Indias</a></i> (General Archive of the Indies) are UNESCO <a href="/wiki/World_Heritage_Site" title="World Heritage Site">World Heritage Sites</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Landmarks">Landmarks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Landmarks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG/220px-El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG/330px-El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG/440px-El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_atardecer_sobre_Santa_Mar%C3%ADa.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Giralda" title="Giralda">Giralda</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Cathedral_of_seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Cathedral of seville">Cathedral of Seville</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seville_Cathedral" title="Seville Cathedral">St. Mary of the See Cathedral</a> was built from 1401–1519 after the <i><a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a></i> on the former site of the city's <a href="/wiki/Mosque" title="Mosque">mosque</a>. It is among the largest of all medieval and <a href="/wiki/Gothic_architecture" title="Gothic architecture">Gothic</a> cathedrals, in terms of both area and volume. The interior is the longest <a href="/wiki/Nave" title="Nave">nave</a> in Spain, and is lavishly decorated, with a large quantity of <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a> evident. La Giralda is a tower attached to the Cathedral that dates back to the twelfth century. It was originally built as part of a mosque when the Moors ruled in Spain and was later added onto by the Christians. Tourists today can climb the tower by walking up a series of ramps that were previously used by officials who rode their horses to the top of the tower. La Giralda gets its name from the weathervane attached to the very top of it, as "gira" means "turning one" in the Spanish language.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a></i> facing the cathedral was developed from a previous Moorish <a href="/wiki/Palace" title="Palace">Palace</a>. Construction was started in 1181 and continued for over 500 years, mainly in the <a href="/wiki/Mud%C3%A9jar" title="Mudéjar">Mudéjar</a> style, but also in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a> style. The popular TV show Game of Thrones has shot many scenes at this location.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Torre_del_Oro" title="Torre del Oro">Torre del Oro</a></i> was built as a <a href="/wiki/Watchtower" title="Watchtower">watchtower</a> and defensive barrier on the river. A chain was strung through the water from the base of the tower to prevent boats from traveling into the river port.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Casa_consistorial_de_Sevilla" title="Casa consistorial de Sevilla">City Hall</a> was built in the 16th century in high <a href="/wiki/Plateresque" title="Plateresque">Plateresque</a> style by master architect <a href="/wiki/Diego_de_Ria%C3%B1o" title="Diego de Riaño">Diego de Riaño</a>. The façade to Plaza Nueva was built in the 19th century in <a href="/wiki/Neoclassical_architecture" title="Neoclassical architecture">Neoclassical</a> style.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_San_Telmo" title="Palace of San Telmo">Palace of San Telmo</a>, formerly the University of Sailors, and later the Seminary, is now the seat for the <a href="/wiki/Andalusian_Autonomous_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Andalusian Autonomous Government">Andalusian Autonomous Government</a>. It is one of the most emblematic buildings of <a href="/wiki/Baroque_architecture" title="Baroque architecture">baroque architecture</a>, mainly to its world-renowned <a href="/wiki/Churrigueresque" title="Churrigueresque">churrigueresque</a> principal façade and the impressive chapel.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Tobacco_Factory" title="Royal Tobacco Factory">Royal Tobacco Factory</a> is housed on the original site of the first tobacco factory in Europe, a vast 18th century building in <a href="/wiki/Baroque" title="Baroque">Baroque</a> style and the purported inspiration for the opera <i>Carmen</i>.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a></i>, in La Encarnación square, is the world's largest wooden structure.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> A monumental umbrella-like building designed by the German architect <a href="/wiki/J%C3%BCrgen_Mayer_(architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Jürgen Mayer (architect)">Jürgen Mayer</a>, finished in 2011. This modern architecture structure houses the central market and an underground archaeological complex. The terrace roof is a city viewpoint.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/General_Archive_of_the_Indies" title="General Archive of the Indies">General Archive of the Indies</a>, is the repository of extremely valuable archival documents illustrating the history of the Spanish Empire in the Americas and the Philippines. The building itself, an unusually serene and Italianate example of Spanish Renaissance architecture, was designed by Juan de Herrera.</p>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Seville)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza de España (Seville)">Plaza de España</a></i>, in Maria Luisa Park (<i>Parque de Maria Luisa</i>), was built by the architect Aníbal González for the 1929 <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Exposition_of_1929" title="Ibero-American Exposition of 1929">Exposición Ibero-Americana</a>. It is an outstanding example of Regionalist Revival Architecture, a bizarre and loftily conceived mixture of diverse historic styles, such as <a href="/wiki/Art_Deco" title="Art Deco">Art Deco</a> and lavishly ornamented with typical glazed tiles.<sup id="cite_ref-sevilla1_40-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sevilla1-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>The neighbourhood of <i><a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville" title="Triana, Seville">Triana</a></i>, situated on the west bank of the <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalquivir River">Guadalquivir River</a>, played an important role in the history of the city and constitutes by itself a folk, monumental and cultural center.</p>
<p>On the other hand, <i><a href="/wiki/Macarena,_Seville" title="Macarena, Seville">La Macarena</a></i> neighbourhood is located on the northern side of the city centre. It contains some important monuments and religious buildings, such as the Museum and Catholic Church of <i>La Macarena</i> or the <i><a href="/wiki/Hospital_de_las_Cinco_Llagas" title="Hospital de las Cinco Llagas">Hospital de las Cinco Llagas</a></i>.</p>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:708px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG" class="image" title="Plaza de España, panoramic view."><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG/700px-Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG" width="700" height="322" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG/1050px-Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4a/Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG/1400px-Paisaje_de_Espa%C3%B1a.JPG 2x" data-file-width="3410" data-file-height="1570" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">

<a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Seville)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza de España (Seville)">Plaza de España</a>, panoramic view.</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg/220px-Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg/330px-Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg/440px-Museo_bellas_artes_2013001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3868" data-file-height="2579" /></a>
