</div>
</div>
<p>The most important art collection of Seville is the <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Fine_Arts_of_Seville" title="Museum of Fine Arts of Seville">Museum of Fine Arts of Seville</a>. It was established in 1835 in the former Convent of <i>La Merced</i>. It holds many masterworks by <a href="/wiki/Bartolom%C3%A9_Esteban_Murillo" title="Bartolomé Esteban Murillo">Murillo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Pacheco" title="Francisco Pacheco">Pacheco</a>, <a href="/wiki/Zurbar%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Zurbarán">Zurbarán</a>, <a href="/wiki/Vald%C3%A9s_Leal" class="mw-redirect" title="Valdés Leal">Valdés Leal</a>, and others masters of the Baroque Sevillian School, containing also Flemish paintings of the 15th and 16th centuries.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg/220px-Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg/330px-Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg/440px-Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pabell%C3%B3n_Mud%C3%A9jar_001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Arts_and_Traditions_of_Sevilla" title="Museum of Arts and Traditions of Sevilla">Museum of Arts and Traditions</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Other museums in Seville are:</p>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Archeological_Museum_of_Seville" title="Archeological Museum of Seville">Archaeological Museum</a>, which contains collections from the <a href="/wiki/Tartessos" title="Tartessos">Tartessian</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hispania_Baetica" title="Hispania Baetica">Roman</a> periods, located in <i>América</i> square at the María Luisa Park.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Museum_of_Arts_and_Traditions_of_Sevilla" title="Museum of Arts and Traditions of Sevilla">Museum of Arts and Traditions</a>, also in América Square, in front of the Archaeological museum.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Monastery_of_Santa_Maria_de_las_Cuevas" title="Monastery of Santa Maria de las Cuevas">Andalusian Contemporary Art Center</a>, situated in the neighbourhood of <a href="/wiki/La_Cartuja,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="La Cartuja, Seville">La Cartuja</a>.</li>
<li>The Naval Museum, housed in the golden <a href="/wiki/Torre_del_Oro" title="Torre del Oro">Torre del Oro</a>, next to the river <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a>.</li>
<li>The Carriages Museum, in the <a href="/wiki/Los_Remedios" title="Los Remedios">Los Remedios</a> neighbourhood.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">Flamenco</a> Art Museum</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Bullfighting" title="Bullfighting">Bullfighting</a> Museum, in the <a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_toros_de_la_Real_Maestranza_de_Caballer%C3%ADa_de_Sevilla" title="Plaza de toros de la Real Maestranza de Caballería de Sevilla">La Maestranza bullring</a></li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Palace_of_the_Countess_of_Lebrija" title="Palace of the Countess of Lebrija">Palace of the Countess of Lebrija</a>, a private collection which contains many of the mosaic floors discovered in the nearby Roman town of <a href="/wiki/Italica" title="Italica">Italica</a>.</li>
<li>The "Centro <a href="/wiki/Vel%C3%A1zquez" class="mw-redirect" title="Velázquez">Velázquez</a>" (Velázquez Centre) located at the Old Priests Hospital in the touristic <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Seville" title="Santa Cruz, Seville">Santa Cruz</a> neighbourhood.</li>
<li>The <i>Antiquarium</i> in <a href="/wiki/Metropol_Parasol" title="Metropol Parasol">Metropol Parasol</a>, an underground museum which exhibits <i>in situ</i> Roman and Muslim remains.</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville#Main_streets.2C_museums_and_landmarks" title="Triana, Seville">Castillo de San Jorge</a></i> (Castle of St. George) is situated near the Triana market, next to the Isabel II bridge. It was the last seat for the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">Spanish Inquisition</a>.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Macarena,_Seville#Monuments_and_landmarks" title="Macarena, Seville">Museum and Treasure of <i>La Macarena</i></a>, where the collection of the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hermandad_de_la_Esperanza_Macarena_(Seville)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Hermandad de la Esperanza Macarena (Seville) (page does not exist)">Macarena brotherhood</a> is exhibited. This exhibition gives visitors an accurate impression of Seville's <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week" title="Holy Week">Seville Holy Week</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/La_Casa_de_la_Ciencia_de_Sevilla_-_Science_Museum" title="La Casa de la Ciencia de Sevilla - Science Museum">La Casa de la Ciencia de Sevilla - Science Museum</a>, opposite the María Luisa Park.</li>
<li>Museum of Pottery in Triana.</li>
<li>Pabellon de la Navegación (Pavilion of Navigation).</li>
</ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Parks_and_gardens">Parks and gardens</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Parks and gardens">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg/220px-Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg/330px-Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/aa/Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg/440px-Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2848" data-file-height="2136" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_-_Sevilla_3.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Pergola in <a href="/wiki/Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="María Luisa Park">María Luisa Park</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Parque_de_Mar%C3%ADa_Luisa" class="mw-redirect" title="Parque de María Luisa">Parque de María Luisa</a></i> (María Luisa Park), is a monumental park built for the 1929 <a href="/wiki/World%27s_Fair" class="mw-redirect" title="World's Fair">World's Fair</a> held in Seville, the <a href="/wiki/Ibero-American_Exposition_of_1929" title="Ibero-American Exposition of 1929">Exposición Ibero-Americana</a>. The so-called <i>Jardines de las Delicias</i> (literally, Delighting Gardens), closer to the river, are part of the <i>Parque de María Luisa</i>.</li>
<li>The Alcázar Gardens, within the grounds of the <i><a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a></i> palace, consist of several sectors developed in different historical styles.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:177px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg/175px-El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg" width="175" height="117" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg/263px-El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/db/El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg/350px-El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_huevo_de_Col%C3%B3n.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <i>Birth of a New Man</i> statue of Christopher Columbus.</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li>The Gardens of Murillo and the Gardens of Catalina de Ribera, both along and outside the South wall of the Alcázar, lie next to the <i>Santa Cruz</i> quarter.</li>
<li>The <i>Parque del Alamillo y San Jerónimo</i>, the largest park in Andalusia, was originally built for <a href="/wiki/Seville_Expo_%2792" title="Seville Expo '92">Seville Expo '92</a> to reproduce the Andalusian native flora. It lines both <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a> shores around the <i>San Jerónimo</i> <a href="/wiki/Meander" title="Meander">meander</a>.</li>
</ul>
<p>The impressive 32-metres-high bronze sculpture, <i>The Birth of a New Man</i> (popularly known as Columbus's Egg, <i>el Huevo de Colón</i>), by the Georgian sculptor <a href="/wiki/Zurab_Tsereteli" title="Zurab Tsereteli">Zurab Tsereteli</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> is located in its northwestern sector.</p>
<ul>
<li>The American Garden, also completed for Expo '92, is in <a href="/wiki/La_Cartuja" class="mw-redirect" title="La Cartuja">La Cartuja</a>. It is a public botanical garden, with a representative collection of American plants donated by different countries on the occasion of the world exposition. Despite its extraordinary botanical value, it remains a mostly abandoned place.</li>
</ul>
<div class="thumb tnone" style="margin-left: auto; margin-right:auto; width:99%; max-width:708px;">
<div class="thumbinner" style="">
<div class="overflowbugx" style="overflow:auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg" class="image" title="The Alcázar Gardens"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg/700px-Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg" width="700" height="254" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg/1050px-Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg/1400px-Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6468" data-file-height="2346" /></a></div>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevilla_Alcazar_03.jpg" title="File:Sevilla Alcazar 03.jpg"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Alcazar_de_Sevilla" class="mw-redirect" title="Alcazar de Sevilla">Alcázar</a> Gardens</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Festivals">Festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg/220px-El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg" width="220" height="243" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg/330px-El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c5/El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg/440px-El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1162" data-file-height="1285" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:El_Gran_Poder_sevillano_por_la_Catedral.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<i>Jesus of the Great Power</i> (<a href="/wiki/Juan_de_Mesa" title="Juan de Mesa">Juan de Mesa</a>, 1620), in the Holy Week <i><a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Seville#Good_Friday_.28Early_Hours.29_La_Madrug.C3.A1" title="Holy Week in Seville">Madrugá</a></i></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Seville" title="Holy Week in Seville"><i>Semana Santa</i> (Holy Week)</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Fair" title="Seville Fair"><i>Feria de Sevilla</i> (Seville Fair)</a>, also known as <i>Feria de Abril</i> (April Fair), are the two most well-known of Seville's festivals. Seville is internationally renowned for the solemn but decorative processions during <a href="/wiki/Easter" title="Easter">Holy Week</a> and the colourful and lively fair held two weeks after. During the Feria, families, businesses and organisations set up <i>casetas</i> (<a href="/wiki/Tent#Marquees_and_larger_tents" title="Tent">marquees</a>) in which they spend the week dancing, drinking, and socialising. Traditionally, women wear elaborate <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a> dresses and men dress in their best suits. The marquees are set up on a permanent fairground in the district of <a href="/wiki/Los_Remedios" title="Los Remedios">Los Remedios</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> in which each street is named after a famous bullfighter.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Gastronomy">Gastronomy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Gastronomy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg/220px-Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg/330px-Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c0/Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg/440px-Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2800" data-file-height="2100" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Gazpacho_Cazuela_Barro.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Andalusian <a href="/wiki/Gazpacho" title="Gazpacho">Gazpacho</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Tapas" title="Tapas">tapas</a></i> scene is one of the main cultural attractions of the city: people go from one bar to another, enjoying small dishes called tapas (literally "lids" or "covers" in Spanish, referring to their probable origin as snacks served on small plates used to cover drinks). Local specialities include fried and grilled seafood (including <a href="/wiki/Squid" title="Squid">squid</a>, <i>choco</i> (<a href="/wiki/Cuttlefish" title="Cuttlefish">cuttlefish</a>), <a href="/wiki/Swordfish" title="Swordfish">swordfish</a>, marinated <a href="/wiki/Squalidae" title="Squalidae">dogfish</a>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Snakelocks_anemone#Gastronomy" title="Snakelocks anemone">ortiguillas</a></i>), grilled and stewed meat, <a href="/wiki/Spinach" title="Spinach">spinach</a> with <a href="/wiki/Chickpea" title="Chickpea">chickpeas</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Jam%C3%B3n_ib%C3%A9rico" title="Jamón ibérico">Jamón ibérico</a></i>, lamb kidneys in sherry sauce, <a href="/wiki/Land_snail#Snails_as_human_food" title="Land snail">snails</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Puchero" title="Puchero">caldo de puchero</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Gazpacho" title="Gazpacho">gazpacho</a></i>. A sandwich known as a <i><a href="/wiki/Serranito" title="Serranito">serranito</a></i> is the typical and popular version of fast food.</p>
<p>Typical desserts from Seville include <i>pestiños</i>, a honey-coated sweet fritter; <i>torrijas</i>, fried slices of bread with honey; <i>roscos fritos</i>, deep-fried sugar-coated ring doughnuts; <i>magdalenas</i> or fairy cakes; <i>yemas de San Leandro</i>,<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> which provide the city's <a href="/wiki/Convent" title="Convent">convents</a> with a source of revenue; and <i><a href="/wiki/Tortas_de_aceite" title="Tortas de aceite">tortas de aceite</a></i>, a thin sugar-coated cake made with olive oil. <i>Polvorones</i> and <i>mantecados</i> are traditional Christmas products, whereas <i>pestiños</i> and <i>torrijas</i> are typically consumed during the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Week_in_Seville" title="Holy Week in Seville">Holy Week</a>.</p>
<p>Bitter <a href="/wiki/Seville_orange" class="mw-redirect" title="Seville orange">Seville oranges</a> grow on trees lining the city streets. Formerly, large quantities were collected and exported to Britain to be used in <a href="/wiki/Marmalade" title="Marmalade">marmalade</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Today the fruit is used predominantly as compost locally, rather than as a foodstuff. According to legend, the Arabs brought the bitter orange to Seville from East Asia via Iraq around the 10th century to beautify and perfume their patios and gardens, as well as to provide shade.<sup id="cite_ref-Nash2005_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Nash2005-44">[44]</a></sup> The flowers of the tree are a source of <a href="/wiki/Neroli_oil" class="mw-redirect" title="Neroli oil">neroli oil</a>, commonly used in <a href="/wiki/Perfumery" class="mw-redirect" title="Perfumery">perfumery</a> and in skin lotions for massage.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfalfa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Alfalfa.jpg/220px-Alfalfa.jpg" width="220" height="109" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Alfalfa.jpg/330px-Alfalfa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Alfalfa.jpg/440px-Alfalfa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3882" data-file-height="1915" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Alfalfa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Street in 'La Alfalfa', neighbourhood known for its important nightlife and its musical scene, beside <a href="/wiki/Alameda_de_Hercules" class="mw-redirect" title="Alameda de Hercules">Alameda</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Arenal,_Seville" title="El Arenal, Seville">El Arenal</a> and <a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville" title="Triana, Seville">Triana</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville had a vibrant rock music scene in the 1970s and 1980s<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> with bands like <a href="/wiki/Triana_(band)" title="Triana (band)">Triana</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alameda_(band)" title="Alameda (band)">Alameda</a> and <a href="/wiki/Smash_(British_band)" title="Smash (British band)">Smash</a>, who fused Andalusia's traditional <a href="/wiki/Flamenco_music" class="mw-redirect" title="Flamenco music">flamenco music</a> with British-style progressive rock. The punk rock group <a href="/wiki/Reincidentes" title="Reincidentes">Reincidentes</a> and indie band <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sr_Chinarro&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sr Chinarro (page does not exist)">Sr Chinarro</a>, as well as singer <a href="/wiki/Kiko_Veneno" title="Kiko Veneno">Kiko Veneno</a>, rose to prominence in the early 1990s. The city's music scene now features rap acts such as <a href="/wiki/SFDK_(band)" title="SFDK (band)">SFDK</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mala_Rodr%C3%ADguez" title="Mala Rodríguez">Mala Rodríguez</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dareysteel" title="Dareysteel">Dareysteel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tote_King" title="Tote King">Tote King</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Dogma_Crew&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Dogma Crew (page does not exist)">Dogma Crew</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Bisley_DeMarra&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Bisley DeMarra (page does not exist)">Bisley DeMarra</a>, <a href="https://es.wikipedia.org/wiki/Haze_(MC)" class="extiw" title="es:Haze (MC)">Haze</a> and <a href="/w/index.php?title=Jesuly&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Jesuly (page does not exist)">Jesuly</a>. Seville's diverse music scene is reflected in the variety of its club-centred nightlife.</p>
<p>The city is also home to many theatres and performance spaces where classical music is performed, including <a href="/wiki/Teatro_Lope_de_Vega,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Teatro Lope de Vega, Seville">Teatro Lope de Vega</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Teatro_La_Maestranza&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Teatro La Maestranza (page does not exist)">Teatro La Maestranza</a>, Teatro Central, the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Real_Alcazar_Gardens&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Real Alcazar Gardens (page does not exist)">Real Alcazar Gardens</a> and the Sala Joaquín Turina.</p>
<p>Despite its name, the <a href="/wiki/Sevillana" class="mw-redirect" title="Sevillana">sevillana</a> dance, commonly presented as <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a>, is not thought to be of Sevillan origin. However, the folksongs called <i><a href="/wiki/Sevillanas" title="Sevillanas">sevillanas</a></i> are authentically Sevillan, as is the four-part dance performed with them. Seville, and most significantly, the western district of <a href="/wiki/Triana,_Seville" title="Triana, Seville">Triana</a>, was a major centre of the development of <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">flamenco</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_(6570969587).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg/220px-Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg/330px-Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg/440px-Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_%286570969587%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_city_at_Christmas_night_(6570969587).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Avenida de la Constitución during <a href="/wiki/Christmas" title="Christmas">Christmas</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville is the most populated city in southern Spain, and has the largest GDP (<a href="/wiki/Gross_Domestic_Product" class="mw-redirect" title="Gross Domestic Product">Gross Domestic Product</a>) of any in Andalusia,<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_de_Sevilla_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_de_Sevilla-45">[45]</a></sup> accounting for one quarter of its total GDP.<sup id="cite_ref-ABC_de_Sevilla_45-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ABC_de_Sevilla-45">[45]</a></sup> All municipalities in the metropolitan area depend directly or indirectly on Seville's economy, while agriculture dominates the economy of the smaller villages, with some industrial activity localised in industrial parks. The <i>Diputacion de Sevilla</i> (Deputation of Seville), with provincial headquarters in the Antiguo Cuartel de Caballería (Old Cavalry Barracks) on Avenida Menendez Pelayo, provides public services to distant villages that they can not provide themselves.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Seville" title="University of Seville">University of Seville</a> and the University Pablo de Olavide are important centres of learning in western Andalusia as they offer a wide range of academic courses; consequently the city has a large number of students from <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">Huelva</a> and <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>.</p>
<p>The economic activity of Seville cannot be detached from the geographical and urban context of the city; the capital of Andalusia is the centre of a growing metropolitan area. Aside from traditional neighbourhoods such as <a href="/wiki/Santa_Cruz,_Seville" title="Santa Cruz, Seville">Santa Cruz</a>, Triana and others, those further away from the centre, such as <a href="/wiki/Nervi%C3%B3n,_Seville" title="Nervión, Seville">Nervión</a>, Sevilla Este, and El Porvenir have seen recent economic growth. Until the economic crisis of 2007, this urban area saw significant population growth and the development of new industrial and commercial parks.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>During this period, availability of infrastructure in the city contributed to the growth of an economy dominated by the service sector,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> but in which industry still holds a considerable place.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg/220px-Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg" width="220" height="332" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg/330px-Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg/440px-Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="4928" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Torre_Sevilla_desde_Puente_de_la_Barqueta.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir_River" class="mw-redirect" title="Guadalquivir River">Guadalquivir River</a>, Schindler Tower and <a href="/wiki/Cajasol_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Cajasol Tower">Sevilla Tower</a> on the Isla de La Cartuja, designed by the architect <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Pelli" title="César Pelli">César Pelli</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The 1990s saw massive growth in investment in infrastructure in Seville, largely due to its hosting of the <a href="/wiki/Seville_Expo_%2792" title="Seville Expo '92">Universal Exposition of Seville</a> in 1992. This economic development of the city and its urban area is supported by good transportation links to other Spanish cities, including a high-speed <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> railway connection to Madrid, and a new international <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pablo Airport">airport</a>.</p>
<p>Seville has the only inland port in Spain, located 80&#160;km (50&#160;mi) from the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a> River. This harbour complex offers access to the Atlantic and the Mediterranean, and allows trade in goods between the south of Spain (Andalusia, <a href="/wiki/Extremadura" title="Extremadura">Extremadura</a>) and Europe, the Middle East and North Africa. The port has undergone reorganisation. Annual <a href="/wiki/Tonnage" title="Tonnage">tonnage</a> rose to 5.3 million tonnes of goods in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Cartuja_93" title="Cartuja 93">Cartuja 93</a> is a research and development park.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> employing 15,000 persons. The <a href="/wiki/Cajasol_Tower" class="mw-redirect" title="Cajasol Tower">Cajasol Tower</a> skyscraper is under construction in the park for the Spanish bank <a href="/wiki/Banca_Civica" title="Banca Civica">Cajasol</a>'s headquarters and offices. The tower was started in March 2008 and is expected to be finished in 2015. With a height of 180.5 metres (592 feet) and 40 <a href="/wiki/Storey" title="Storey">floors</a>, it will be the tallest building in <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>.</p>
<p>Seville has conference facilities, including the Congress Palace. Its <i>Parque Tecnológico y Aeronáutico Aerópolis</i> (Technological and Aeronautical Park) is focused on the aircraft industry. Outside of Seville are nine <a href="/wiki/PS20_solar_power_towers" class="mw-redirect" title="PS20 solar power towers">PS20 solar power towers</a> which use the city's sunny weather to provide most of it with clean and renewable energy.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg/220px-HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg/330px-HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg/440px-HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4183" data-file-height="2745" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:HEINEKEN_MARCOROJO179.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Heineken" title="Heineken">Heineken</a> brewery in Seville</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research_and_development">Research and development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Research and development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i>Consejo Superior de Investigaciones Científicas en Sevilla</i> (CSIC) is based in the former <a href="/wiki/Pavilion_of_Peru,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Pavilion of Peru, Seville">Pavilion of Peru</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Maria_Luisa_Park" title="Maria Luisa Park">Maria Luisa Park</a>. In April 2008 the city council of Seville provided a grant to renovate the building to create the <i>Casa de la Ciencia</i> (<a href="/wiki/Science_Center,_Seville" class="mw-redirect" title="Science Center, Seville">Science Center</a>) to encourage popular interest in science.<sup id="cite_ref-Gordillo1998_52-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Gordillo1998-52">[52]</a></sup> The internationally recognised company <i>Neocodex</i> has its headquarters in Seville; it maintains the first and largest <a href="/wiki/DNA_bank" title="DNA bank">DNA bank</a> in Spain and has made significant contributions to scientific research in genetics.<sup id="cite_ref-Genetic_Engineering_.26_Biotechnology_News:_GEN._53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Genetic_Engineering_.26_Biotechnology_News:_GEN.-53">[53]</a></sup> Seville is also considered an important technological and research centre for renewable energy and the aeronautics industry.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<p>The output of the research centres in Sevillan universities working in tandem with city government, and the numerous local technology companies, have made Seville a leader among Spanish cities in technological <a href="/wiki/Research_and_development" title="Research and development">research and development</a>. The <i>Parque Científico Tecnológico Cartuja 93</i> is a nexus of private and public investment in various fields of research.<sup id="cite_ref-Moncl.C3.BAsFraga2006_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Moncl.C3.BAsFraga2006-56">[56]</a></sup></p>
<p>Principal fields of innovation and research are: telecommunications, new technologies, biotechnology (with applications in local agricultural practices), environment and renewable energy.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus">Bus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Bus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seville is served by the TUSSAM <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.tussam.es/">(Transportes Urbanos de Sevilla)</a> <a href="/wiki/Transit_bus" title="Transit bus">bus</a> network which runs buses throughout the city. The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.consorciotransportes-sevilla.com/">Consorcio de Transportes de Sevilla</a> communicates by bus with all the satellite towns of Seville.</p>
<p>Two bus stations serve transportation between surrounding areas and other cities: <i>Plaza de Armas</i> Station, with destinations north and west, and <i>Prado de San Sebastián</i> Station, covering routes to the south and east. <i>Plaza de Armas</i> station has direct bus lines to many Spanish cities and with <a href="/wiki/Lisbon" title="Lisbon">Lisbon</a>, in Portugal.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Metro">Metro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Metro">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Seville_metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Seville metro">Seville metro</a> ("Metro de Sevilla" in Spanish) is a light metro network serving the city of Seville and its <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_area" title="Metropolitan area">metropolitan area</a>. The system is totally independent of any other rail or street traffic. All stations were built with <a href="/wiki/Platform_screen_doors" title="Platform screen doors">platform screen doors</a>.</p>
<p>It was the sixth Metro system to be built in Spain, after those in <a href="/wiki/Madrid_Metro" title="Madrid Metro">Madrid</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barcelona_Metro" title="Barcelona Metro">Barcelona</a>, <a href="/wiki/Valencia_Metro_(Spain)" class="mw-redirect" title="Valencia Metro (Spain)">Valencia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Metro_Bilbao" title="Metro Bilbao">Bilbao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Palma_de_Mallorca_Metro" class="mw-redirect" title="Palma de Mallorca Metro">Palma de Mallorca</a>. Currently, it is the fifth biggest Metro company in Spain by number of passengers carried (more than 12,000,000 in 2009).</p>
<p>The metro of Sevilla has 1 line with 22 stations and is currently expanding, with 3 more different lines projected.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tram">Tram</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Tram">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_Metro_Train.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Seville_Metro_Train.JPG/220px-Seville_Metro_Train.JPG" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Seville_Metro_Train.JPG/330px-Seville_Metro_Train.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/Seville_Metro_Train.JPG/440px-Seville_Metro_Train.JPG 2x" data-file-width="6000" data-file-height="4000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Seville_Metro_Train.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/MetroCentro_(Seville)" title="MetroCentro (Seville)">MetroCentro</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/MetroCentro_(Seville)" title="MetroCentro (Seville)">MetroCentro</a> is a surface <a href="/wiki/Tram" title="Tram">tramway</a> serving the centre of the city. It began operating in October 2007.</p>
<p>The service has just five stops: Plaza Nueva, Archivo de Indias, Puerta de Jerez, Prado de San Sebastián and San Bernardo, all as part of <i>Phase I</i> of the project. It is expected to be extended to Santa Justa <a href="/wiki/Alta_Velocidad_Espa%C3%B1ola" class="mw-redirect" title="Alta Velocidad Española">AVE</a> station, including four new stops: San Francisco Javier, Eduardo Dato, Luis de Morales and Santa Justa. This extension was postponed although the City Council had made expanding the metro lines a priority.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Train">Train</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Train">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <b>Santa Justa Train Station</b> is served by the <a href="/wiki/AVE" title="AVE">AVE</a> <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a> system, operated by the Spanish state-owned rail company <a href="/wiki/Renfe" class="mw-redirect" title="Renfe">Renfe</a>. A five-line commuter rail service (<i><a href="/wiki/Cercan%C3%ADas_Sevilla" title="Cercanías Sevilla">Cercanías</a></i>) joins the city with the Metropolitan area. Seville is on the <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.redciudadesave.es/">Red Ciudades AVE</a>, a net created with Seville next to 17 major cities of <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a> with <a href="/wiki/High-speed_rail" title="High-speed rail">high-speed rail</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bicycle">Bicycle</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Bicycle">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevici.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sevici.jpg/220px-Sevici.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sevici.jpg/330px-Sevici.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Sevici.jpg/440px-Sevici.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sevici.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sevici" title="Sevici">Sevici</a> Bicycle station</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Sevici" title="Sevici">Sevici</a> <a href="/w/index.php?title=Community_bicycle_programme&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Community bicycle programme (page does not exist)">community bicycle programme</a> has integrated bicycles into the public transport network. Bicycles are available for hire around the city at low cost and green bicycle lanes can be seen on most major streets. The number of people using bicycles as a means of transport in Seville has increased substantially in recent years, multiplying tenfold from 2006 to 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup> As of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, an estimated 9 percent of all mechanized trips in the city (and 5.6 percent of all trips including those on foot) are made by bicycle.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<p>The city council signed a contract with the multinational corporation <a href="/wiki/JCDecaux" title="JCDecaux">JCDecaux</a>, an outdoor advertising company. The public bicycle rental system is financed by a local advertising operator in return for the city signing over a 10-year licence to exploit citywide billboards. The overall scheme is called Cyclocity<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> by JCDecaux, but each city's system is branded under an individual name.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Airport">Airport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Airport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vueling,_San_Pablo_Airport,_Sevilla,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2015.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG/220px-Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG/330px-Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/63/Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG/440px-Vueling%2C_San_Pablo_Airport%2C_Sevilla%2C_Espa%C3%B1a%2C_2015.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4000" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vueling,_San_Pablo_Airport,_Sevilla,_Espa%C3%B1a,_2015.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Several planes at <a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pablo Airport">San Pablo Airport</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/San_Pablo_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="San Pablo Airport">San Pablo Airport</a> is the main airport for Seville and is <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">Andalusia</a>'s second busiest airport, after <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Ruiz_Picasso_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Pablo Ruiz Picasso International Airport">Malaga</a>. The airport handled 4,051,392 passengers and just under 5,000 tonnes of cargo in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-stats_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-stats-60">[60]</a></sup> It has one <a href="/wiki/Airport_terminal" title="Airport terminal">terminal</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Runway" title="Runway">runway</a>.</p>
<p>It is one of many bases for the Spanish low cost carrier <a href="/wiki/Vueling_Airlines" class="mw-redirect" title="Vueling Airlines">Vueling</a>, and from November 2010 <a href="/wiki/Ryanair" title="Ryanair">Ryanair</a> will base two aircraft at the airport.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Port">Port</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Port">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seville is the only commercial river port of Spain, and the only inland city in the country where cruise ships can arrive in the historical centre. On 21 August 2012, the Muelle de las Delicias, controlled by the Port Authority of Seville, hosted the cruise ship <a href="/wiki/Azamara_Journey" title="Azamara Journey">Azamara Journey</a> for two days, the largest ship ever to visit the town. This vessel belongs to the shipping company Royal Caribbean and can accommodate up to 700 passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Roads">Roads</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Roads">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Seville has one ring road, the SE-30, which connects with the dual carriageway of the south, the A-4, that directly communicates the city with <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A1diz" title="Cádiz">Cádiz</a>, <a href="/wiki/C%C3%B3rdoba,_Andalusia" title="Córdoba, Andalusia">Cordoba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a>. Also there is another dual carriageway, the A-92, linking the city with <a href="/wiki/Estepa" title="Estepa">Estepa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Antequera" title="Antequera">Antequera</a>, <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Guadix" title="Guadix">Guadix</a> and <a href="/wiki/Almeria" class="mw-redirect" title="Almeria">Almeria</a>. The A-49 links Seville with <a href="/wiki/Huelva" title="Huelva">Huelva</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Algarve" title="Algarve">Algarve</a> in the south of <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:FCOM.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/FCOM.jpg/220px-FCOM.jpg" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/FCOM.jpg/330px-FCOM.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/FCOM.jpg/440px-FCOM.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3929" data-file-height="3096" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:FCOM.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Faculty of Communication (<a href="/wiki/University_of_Seville" title="University of Seville">University of Seville</a>)</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville is home to three public universities: the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Seville" title="University of Seville">University of Seville</a>, founded in 1505, the <a href="/wiki/Pablo_de_Olavide_University" title="Pablo de Olavide University">Pablo de Olavide University</a>, founded in 1997, and the <a href="/wiki/International_University_of_Andalusia" class="mw-redirect" title="International University of Andalusia">International University of Andalusia</a>, founded in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup></p>
<p>Additionally, there is the School of Hispanic American Studies, founded in 1942, the <a href="/wiki/Men%C3%A9ndez_Pelayo_International_University" title="Menéndez Pelayo International University">Menéndez Pelayo International University</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Santander,_Cantabria" class="mw-redirect" title="Santander, Cantabria">Santander</a>, which operates branch campuses in Seville, and <a href="/wiki/Loyola_University_Andalusia" title="Loyola University Andalusia">Loyola University Andalusia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The University Loyola Andalucía is a Jesuits private university located in the campus of Palmas Altas, close to the Seville Port. The university offers a wide range of social science degrees, such as Business Administration, International Relations, Economics, for instance, as well as, engineering and law degrees, and postgraduate degrees. The educational institution was founded 4 years ago, in 2013, but its educational background has been existing since 1963, with the campus of Córdoba in the past ETEA University. Currently, this university is formed by two different campus located in Seville and Cordoba. The institution offers a high-quality formation thanks to its formed professors. The internalization is an important aspect of this university which maintain a large number of agreements with different universities around the world. Within all the different program this University offers, the Dual Business Degree is the most prestigious one. This international program provides, for only 20 business students each year, the possibility to obtain a Business Administration degree by the Universidad Loyola Andalucía as well as by the Loyola University of Chicago. During the freshmen year, these students spend all the academic year studying on the Campus of Seville or Córdoba. The second year, they spend their first semester studying in the John Felice Rome Center, which is a university center of the Loyola University of Chicago located in Rome. Then, the second semester the students return to Spain and continue there their studies. During the junior year, they travel to Chicago and studying in Loyola University of Chicago for the whole year. Finally, in the senior year, the students return to Spain and finish their careers there. Apart from the great academic qualification, explained before, this program provides to their candidates a fantastic opportunity to develop themselves as an adult person, and opening their minds for the currently global reality.</p>
<p>International primary and secondary schools:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lyc%C3%A9e_Fran%C3%A7ais_de_S%C3%A9ville" title="Lycée Français de Séville">Lycée Français de Séville</a> (French school)</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Deutsche_Schule_Sevilla" title="Deutsche Schule Sevilla">Deutsche Schule Sevilla</a> (German school)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=St._George%27s_British_School_of_Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="St. George's British School of Seville (page does not exist)">St. George's British School of Seville</a></li>
</ul>
<p>Seville is also home to many international schools and colleges that cater to American students who come to study abroad</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg/220px-Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg/330px-Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg/440px-Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1300" data-file-height="863" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Panoramio_-_V%26A_Dudush_-_Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_57_619.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ol%C3%ADmpico_de_La_Cartuja" class="mw-redirect" title="Estadio Olímpico de La Cartuja">La Cartuja Olympic Stadium</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Seville is the hometown of two rival <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">association football</a> teams: <a href="/wiki/Real_Betis" title="Real Betis">Real Betis Balompié</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sevilla_FC" title="Sevilla FC">Sevilla Fútbol Club</a>, both teams are playing in the <a href="/wiki/Liga_BBVA" class="mw-redirect" title="Liga BBVA">Liga BBVA</a>. Both teams have only won the league once each: Betis in 1935 and Sevilla in 1946.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> Only Sevilla has won European competitions, winning consecutive <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="UEFA Cup">UEFA Cup</a> finals in <a href="/wiki/2006_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2006 UEFA Cup Final">2006</a> and <a href="/wiki/2007_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2007 UEFA Cup Final">2007</a><sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/UEFA_Europa_League" title="UEFA Europa League">UEFA Europa League</a> in <a href="/wiki/2014_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2014 UEFA Europa League Final">2014</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/2015_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2015 UEFA Europa League Final">2015</a> and <a href="/wiki/2016_UEFA_Europa_League_Final" title="2016 UEFA Europa League Final">2016</a>. Sevilla's stadium, the <a href="/wiki/Estadio_Ram%C3%B3n_S%C3%A1nchez_Pizju%C3%A1n" class="mw-redirect" title="Estadio Ramón Sánchez Pizjuán">Ramón Sánchez Pizjuán</a>, was a venue during the <a href="/wiki/1982_FIFA_World_Cup" title="1982 FIFA World Cup">1982 FIFA World Cup</a><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> and four years later hosted the <a href="/wiki/1986_European_Cup_Final" title="1986 European Cup Final">1986 European Cup Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> Seville's <a href="/wiki/Estadio_de_La_Cartuja" title="Estadio de La Cartuja">Olympic Stadium</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Isla_de_La_Cartuja" title="Isla de La Cartuja">Isla de La Cartuja</a> was the venue for the <a href="/wiki/2003_UEFA_Cup_Final" title="2003 UEFA Cup Final">2003 UEFA Cup Final</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>Seville housed the tennis <a href="/wiki/Davis_Cup" title="Davis Cup">Davis Cup</a> final in 2004 and 2011, and the <a href="/wiki/1999_World_Championships_in_Athletics" title="1999 World Championships in Athletics">7th Athletics World Championships</a>. The city unsuccessfully bid for the <a href="/wiki/2004_Summer_Olympics" title="2004 Summer Olympics">2004</a><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/2008_Summer_Olympics" title="2008 Summer Olympics">2008 Summer Olympics</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> for which the 60,000-seat <a href="/wiki/Estadio_de_La_Cartuja" title="Estadio de La Cartuja">Estadio de La Cartuja</a> was designed to stage. Seville has one important basketball club, the <a href="/wiki/CB_Sevilla" title="CB Sevilla">CB Sevilla</a>, that plays in <a href="/wiki/ACB_League" class="mw-redirect" title="ACB League">ACB League</a>. Seville's <a href="/wiki/Guadalquivir" title="Guadalquivir">Guadalquivir</a> river is one of only three <a href="/wiki/International_Rowing_Federation" title="International Rowing Federation">FISA</a> approved international training centres for <a href="/wiki/Rowing_(sport)" title="Rowing (sport)">rowing (sport)</a> and the only one in Spain; the <a href="/wiki/2002_World_Rowing_Championships" title="2002 World Rowing Championships">2002 World Rowing Championships</a> and the <a href="/wiki/2013_European_Rowing_Championships" title="2013 European Rowing Championships">2013 European Rowing Championships</a> were held there.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_fiction">In fiction</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: In fiction">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Picaresque_novel" title="Picaresque novel">picaresque novel</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Rinconete_y_Cortadillo" title="Rinconete y Cortadillo">Rinconete y Cortadillo</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">Miguel de Cervantes</a> takes place in the city of Seville.</li>
<li>The novel <i><a href="/wiki/La_Femme_et_le_pantin" class="mw-redirect" title="La Femme et le pantin">La Femme et le pantin</a></i>, ("The Woman and the Puppet") (1898) by <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Lou%C3%BFs" title="Pierre Louÿs">Pierre Louÿs</a>, adapted for film several times, is set mainly in Seville.</li>
<li>Seville is the setting for the legend of <a href="/wiki/Don_Juan" title="Don Juan">Don Juan</a> (inspired by the real aristocrat <a href="/w/index.php?title=Don_Miguel_de_Ma%C3%B1ara&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Don Miguel de Mañara (page does not exist)">Don Miguel de Mañara</a>) on the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Paseo_Alcalde_Marqu%C3%A9s_de_Contadero&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Paseo Alcalde Marqués de Contadero (page does not exist)">Paseo Alcalde Marqués de Contadero</a></li>
<li>Seville is the primary setting of many operas, the best known of which are <a href="/wiki/Georges_Bizet" title="Georges Bizet">Bizet</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Carmen_(opera)" class="mw-redirect" title="Carmen (opera)">Carmen</a></i> (based on <a href="/wiki/Prosper_Merim%C3%A9e" class="mw-redirect" title="Prosper Merimée">Mérimée</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Carmen_(novella)" title="Carmen (novella)">novella</a>), <a href="/wiki/Gioachino_Rossini" title="Gioachino Rossini">Rossini</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Barber_of_Seville" title="The Barber of Seville">The Barber of Seville</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Giuseppe_Verdi" title="Giuseppe Verdi">Verdi</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/La_forza_del_destino" title="La forza del destino">La forza del destino</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_van_Beethoven" title="Ludwig van Beethoven">Beethoven</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Fidelio" title="Fidelio">Fidelio</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Wolfgang_Amadeus_Mozart" title="Wolfgang Amadeus Mozart">Mozart</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Giovanni" title="Don Giovanni">Don Giovanni</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Marriage_of_Figaro" title="The Marriage of Figaro">The Marriage of Figaro</a></i>, and <a href="/wiki/Prokofiev" class="mw-redirect" title="Prokofiev">Prokofiev</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Betrothal_in_a_Monastery" title="Betrothal in a Monastery">Betrothal in a Monastery</a></i>.</li>
<li>Seville is the setting of the novel "The Seville Communion" by <a href="/wiki/Arturo_P%C3%A9rez-Reverte" title="Arturo Pérez-Reverte">Arturo Pérez-Reverte</a>.</li>
<li>Seville is both the location and setting for much of the 1985 <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Who" title="Doctor Who">Doctor Who</a> television serial <a href="/wiki/The_Two_Doctors" title="The Two Doctors">The Two Doctors</a>.</li>
<li>Seville is also used as one of the locations in Dan Brown's "<a href="/wiki/Digital_Fortress" title="Digital Fortress">Digital Fortress</a>".</li>
<li>Seville is one of the settings in <i><a href="/wiki/Jostein_Gaarder" title="Jostein Gaarder">Jostein Gaarder</a>'</i>s book "The Orange Girl" ("Appelsinpiken").</li>
<li>Seville is the hometown of the two main characters in the 2000 film <i><a href="/wiki/The_Road_to_El_Dorado" title="The Road to El Dorado">The Road to El Dorado</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/DreamWorks_Pictures" class="mw-redirect" title="DreamWorks Pictures">DreamWorks Pictures</a>. Miguel and Tulio are con artists that stow away on a ship bound for the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> and win a map for the fabled lost city of gold, <a href="/wiki/El_Dorado" title="El Dorado">El Dorado</a> and are invariably seen as gods by the locals.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Arthur_Koestler" title="Arthur Koestler">Arthur Koestler</a>'s book <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Testament" title="Spanish Testament">Spanish Testament</a> is based on the writer's experiences while held in the Seville prison, under a sentence of death, during the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Civil_War" title="Spanish Civil War">Spanish Civil War</a>.</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Robert_Wilson_(crime_novelist)" title="Robert Wilson (crime novelist)">Robert Wilson's</a> police novel <i>The Hidden Assassins</i> (2006) concerns a terrorist incident in Seville and the political context thereof, with much local colour. Note also his title <i>The Blind Man of Seville</i> (2004).</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Sevilla)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza de España (Sevilla)">Plaza de España</a></i> in the <i>Parque de María Luisa</i> appears in George Lucas' <a href="/wiki/Star_Wars:_Episode_II_%E2%80%93_Attack_of_the_Clones" title="Star Wars: Episode II – Attack of the Clones">Star Wars: Episode II – Attack of the Clones</a> as well as in <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i> as the British Army HQ in <a href="/wiki/Cairo" title="Cairo">Cairo</a>, while the courtyard was the <a href="/wiki/Hotel_Alfonso_XIII" title="Hotel Alfonso XIII">King Alfonso XIII Hotel</a>.</li>
<li>The <i>Plaza of the Americas</i> also appeared in <i>Lawrence</i>, substituting for <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Mann" title="Anthony Mann">Anthony Mann</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/El_Cid" title="El Cid">El Cid</a></i>. It would also serve as the Palace of <a href="/wiki/Vladek_Sheybal" title="Vladek Sheybal">Vladek Sheybal</a>'s Bashaw in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Wind_and_the_Lion" title="The Wind and the Lion">The Wind and the Lion</a></i> (1975) (including the memorable attack scene by the US Marines.)</li>
<li>The <i><a href="/wiki/Plaza_de_Espa%C3%B1a_(Sevilla)" class="mw-redirect" title="Plaza de España (Sevilla)">Plaza de España</a></i> in the <i>Parque de María Luisa</i> appears in the movie The Dictator, starring <a href="/wiki/Sacha_Baron_Cohen" title="Sacha Baron Cohen">Sacha Baron Cohen</a>, as the palace of the dictator Aladeen.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/Alc%C3%A1zar_of_Seville" title="Alcázar of Seville">Alcázar</a> and other sites appear in the television series <a href="/wiki/Game_of_Thrones" title="Game of Thrones">Game of Thrones</a>, in the cities of <i>Dorne</i>.</li>
</ul>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Twin_towns_and_sister_cities">Twin towns and sister cities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Twin towns and sister cities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_twin_towns_and_sister_cities_in_Spain" title="List of twin towns and sister cities in Spain">List of twin towns and sister cities in Spain</a></div>
<p>Seville is <a href="/wiki/Twin_towns_and_sister_cities" title="Twin towns and sister cities">twinned</a> with the following cities:<sup id="cite_ref-Seville_Information_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seville_Information-73">[73]</a></sup> The relationship between Seville and Kansas City is due to a small replica of the Giralda tower, Sevilla's cathedral belltower, that exists in Kansas City.</p>

<tr valign="top">
<td>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)"><img alt="Georgia (country)" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/23px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/35px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Flag_of_Georgia.svg/45px-Flag_of_Georgia.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Signagi" title="Signagi">Signagi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> (1999)</li>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/France" title="France"><img alt="France" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/23px-Flag_of_France.svg.png" width="23" height="15" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/35px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/c/c3/Flag_of_France.svg/45px-Flag_of_France.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="900" data-file-height="600" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Angers" title="Angers">Angers</a>, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, since 2000<sup id="cite_ref-Seville_Information_73-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seville_Information-73">[73]</a></sup></li>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Partnerships">Partnerships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=44" title="Edit section: Partnerships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul>
<li><span class="flagicon"><a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland"><img alt="Poland" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/23px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png" width="23" height="14" class="thumbborder" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/35px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/1/12/Flag_of_Poland.svg/46px-Flag_of_Poland.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="800" /></a></span> <a href="/wiki/Krak%C3%B3w" title="Kraków">Kraków</a>, <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> (2002)<sup id="cite_ref-Seville_Information_73-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Seville_Information-73">[73]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Krak.C3.B3w_82-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Krak.C3.B3w-82">[82]</a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Titles">Titles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Seville&amp;action=edit&amp;section=45" title="Edit section: Titles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Seville has been given titles by Spanish monarchs and heads of state throughout its history.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><b>Very Noble</b>, by King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_III_of_Castile" title="Ferdinand III of Castile">Ferdinand III of Castile</a> after his reconquest of the city.</li>
<li><b>Very Loyal</b>, by King <a href="/wiki/Alfonso_X_of_Castile" title="Alfonso X of Castile">Alfonso X of Castile</a> for supporting him against a rebellion. See also the Motto "NO8DO".</li>
<li><b>Very Heroic</b>, by King <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_VII_of_Spain" title="Ferdinand VII of Spain">Ferdinand VII of Spain</a> by Royal Document on 13 October 1817 for support against the French invasion.</li>
<li><b>Invictus</b> (Invincible in <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a>), by Queen <a href="/wiki/Isabella_II_of_Spain" title="Isabella II of Spain">Isabella II of Spain</a> for the city's resistance against General Van Halen's asedium and bombing in 1843.</li>
<li><b>Mariana</b>, by General <a href="/wiki/Francisco_Franco" title="Francisco Franco">Francisco Franco</a> in 1946 for the city's devotion to the Virgin Mary.</li>
</ul>

									<div id="p-personal" role="navigation" class="" aria-labelledby="p-personal-label">
